Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the sinews pull quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this treatment and does not come out, order the nurse to wet her left hand in oil of cedar or marsh mallow juice, and then insert it into the nature (body).
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	And seek the sinew; and when she has found it, grasp it and pull it slowly and directly, so that the patient does not wince at the extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but she must move it lightly to the right and left, and then pull; it will come out and become detached.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the patient's mouth is too tight, we have mentioned the cure of making them sneeze and using fumigation of herbs.
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it doesn't leave any of what we have said, make sure not to pull too hard;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary for the one who is at the opening of the wound to be tied to the thigh of the woman, and then apply a suppository of theriac;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	it will cause it to suppurate and heal, and it will come out; but nevertheless, when it suppurates, a bad smell comes to the stomach and head, and wounds the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Then it is necessary to use appropriate fumigations for that person: some of the ancients have tried fumigation of watercress and dried figs.[translated by user-defi12345]
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument used to fumigate the woman for the retention of periods and after childbirth is as follows:[translated by user-defi12345]
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it looks similar to a dog, and one puts the head gently in its place, and the shoulders wide over the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And let the fumigation be above the coals, and the blister until it is burnt, and start with a new one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation.[i](Note: In medieval medical texts, "piercing the foundation" usually refers to performing an enema.)
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have their foundation pierced, but instead it is stopped up with a fine probe.[^1](Note: In medieval medical texts, "piercing the foundation" usually refers to performing an enema.)[^1]: In this context, "fondement" likely refers to the anus.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that probe in its place, and not with a sharp instrument, and ensure that she does not touch the ligature.[^1](Note: In this context, "syfac" likely refers to an object used to block the anus, similar to a suppository.)[^1]: The term "ligature" may refer to any material or device used to tie or bind something in place. Here, it likely refers to the tool used to hold the probe in place.[^2](Note: In medieval medical texts, "piercing the foundation" usually refers to performing an enema.)[^2]: The term "fondement" likely refers to the anus.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place a wet cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then apply the ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you fear that it will suppurate, place a piece of wood into the wound, and leave it in for several days, and remove it when the child wants to go to the chamber (or: move around).
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this blockage is caused by a sudden closing of a wound or an abscess; in that case, it should be covered and treated, as we have said with the piece of wood.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the rectum (or: of the anus)
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from below the rectum are swellings and grow larger as they appear next to the anus or in a space of two fingers' width.
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if there is a fistula or several; and when this swelling has been present for a long time, work on it, and still there is whitish moisture or thin pus,
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are recognized by the fact that there is discharge or windiness when the patient passes gas, and perhaps also in urination.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that reach to the bladder, and to the middle of the penis; and they extend to the joint of the thigh, and to the navel of the cow.[Note: The translation of "nout de la kowe" is uncertain as it is unclear what body part "kowe" refers to. It could also be translated as "navel of the calf".]
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one recognizes a persistent fistula in the anus, and not persistent.[Note: The translation of "persant" is uncertain as it is unclear what it means for a fistula to be "persistent" or not. It could also be translated as "deep" or "superficial".]
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and this is done by inserting your index finger into the anus, and inserting a thin needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no bending.[Note: The word "aguille" can refer to any kind of sharp, pointed object, not just a modern-day medical needle.][Stopping here for now.]
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is curvature, insert a slender stake of wood, or a horse's hair, until you feel the stake or the hair at your finger.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	And if you do not feel it, and no purging or wind escapes from the opening, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it did not penetrate; so hurry to treat it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has penetrated to the bladder or to the conduit of urine, if urine leaks out and it cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it has pierced to the joint of the thigh, then the stake comes out at the spot.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twist and the origin of the pain around it, then it is already bent, and neither medicine nor ointment helps.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And in these Persian fistulas, there is no cure except for labor and the foolishness of arrogant doctors who meddle with it.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In that which is not Persian and not old, there is hope of health through iron, as I have proven.[Note: The translation "through iron" is an interpretation of the word "fer" in this context. It could also mean "iron-made tool", but the exact meaning may depend on the context of the medical procedure that follows.]
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and the patient lies in your hands on their back; they lift their legs up to their thighs, and have their thighs inclined towards their stomach.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	Then insert an iron probe (or wooden if there is twisting) until you know where the probe goes.[Note: The word "tente" means tent in modern French, but here it refers to a medical probe used for exploration of bodily orifices or wounds. The word "arain" means iron and "plonc" means wood in Old French.]
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around the groin, you should insert your index finger there,
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and if you then feel that the tendon has been pierced, and the syphac or flesh is exposed where you have inserted your finger, know that it has been transfixed;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	do not work on it anymore as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	It is also said that some can be healed, but this happens rarely;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	And the help that is provided is to heat the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before;[
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and place it very hot in the fistula, until it reaches the base; and do this twice or thrice, until you are sure that the charred parts, which resemble a bird's feather, are burned.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	And then cure it with moist bandages smeared with butter, until the char comes out; then cure it with a healing ointment that removes char and heals wounds.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is healed in this way, that is good. But if it cannot be healed otherwise;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	And if the bandage enters and does not reach the finger at the base, but instead there is a thick covering of char or abscess between your finger and the bandage, and you see the fistula following the thick covering of the wound;[IT] et se il est ainsi sané, c’est bien. Mais se ce n’est pas ainsi, et que la fistule soit encore plaine de chars, et ne puet on venir a le voie qui sana, si doit on faire tel remede come je vos dirai:
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	Start by cutting from the beginning of the fistula and pushing the bandage further in, then use the cautery to burn it until you reach the end of the bandage.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	And the abscess will be drained and will fall; then clean away the rotten flesh that looks like a bird's feather, and let nothing of it remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood overpowers you and flows between you and the procedure, cauterize it with fire or a medicinal styptic.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cautery brings about two good things: namely, the burning of the adhered flesh and the staunching of blood and drying of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	Then the treatment of damp abscesses with butter or ground-up herbs, until the area dries out and the burned flesh comes out in the pus;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then treat the wound with incarnating ointments that cause hardening of the flesh, and let the medicines be dry.[translated by Adam S.]
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not come back again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes to the depth of the fundament, and is removed from the body, place your finger in the opening and feel it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the head (of the fistula), and between two there is tissue or syphilitic chancre or flesh, or it is about to break through, then there is no other remedy but one of three methods by faith and hope in their administration.
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if possible, you place a probe and treat it as in the first instance.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	but do not go too deep, so that you do not cut the ligament which holds the foundation, and cause eliminations through it without control.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then cure it, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it since it is cut next to the foundation, using a tent or another pointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then clean the cavity in the wound as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then work on healing the wound and keeping the fistula outside of the foundation; it will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes fistulas are like this: it is when you insert the tent in the fistula, and it is next to the foundation by the skin above it,[
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	take a tent peg pierced at the top in this way:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert a twisted wire through (the hole of) the two (prongs), and push the tent peg all the way to the top of the fistula.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it (the fistula) is perforated in the margin of the anus inside, then pull out the wire from this hole, so that you push your finger into the anus;[text](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/en/fistule)[/text] : fístule féminin
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and pull the head of the wire, and bring the two edges together, and press one against the other, and leave it for one or two days;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and keeps it taut until the son ties the strings that are between two, and separated.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then treats the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because one should not at all make the incision cover so deeply and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the pointed spatula with which one makes the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	"And on the other hand, no, because one does not cut that which should not be cut, as you can see here:"
des emorroydes	"of hemorrhoids"
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Hemorrhoids come in two forms: they are inside the anus, like a seed of resin, and there are both small and large ones, and they cause constant bleeding.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	And some are outside the anus and at the opening of the anus; but those that are outside cause little moisture.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	And still, sometimes there is a little yellow water or a little blood, and they have the color of the body.[
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the care of those who have them in the bowels, so you should instruct the patient to strain when going to the chamber, until the feces come out and are visible.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	and if you hurry, and pierce it with pincers or hold it with your fingernail, then cut it at its roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the hooks cannot hold them because of moisture, take a piece of cloth or cotton or camlet,
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and pull them out with your fingers, then cut it off and powder over it some hot powders that are available instead of the cautery.[STHILDE] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or cauterize it as it is said in the chapter of cautery, and then treat it with other treatments until it heals.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundation(s) cannot come out, purge the patient with a bitter and harsh enema to cleanse what is in the rectum, so that it may come out openly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the patient can defecate, and if the feces are outside of the rectum, then the treatment is easy;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and this is done by taking hold of them with your fingernail or tweezers, cutting them, then treating as we have said until it is healed, and that the incision by iron is feared;
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is necessary that you prepare the suture in this manner: take a twisted thread and place it on a needle, then pull the thread over and make the needle penetrate from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread underneath the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and let it be of a large enough width; pull the thread tight, then knot the thread and remove the needle, and do the same with all the others, leaving one to tie off any excess blood.
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then place on the wound a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote, and place it on the wound, and instruct the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it in place until he urinates, and when they have fallen off, cure the wound with ointment and other treatments, until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	with drying of pus or wound.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	It often happens that there is drying of pus in the intestines, due to constrictions of nature, and when the illness is old and no medicine helps.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	Therefore, you must scrape off with the tip of a spatula or your fingernail the skin on top, so that it does not become moistened;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then cure it until it is solid as it should be;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot become solid, then repeat the shaving even stronger than before, until it heals well and is scarred.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	shivering[INT] de fièvre et de froit
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A formica (anthill) is a small, hollowed-out appearance in the body that goes very deep.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And sometimes it is found frozen, and it feels like a dead chill, and it spreads throughout the body, and more so in the hands than in other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a reed from an ostrich feather, or a strong swallow feather, and place it on the chill, until the circle encompasses the entire chill.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then turn your hand around the entire reed until you have scraped all around the chill, and push it in deep, and extract the chill from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do this with a reed of iron or steel in this manner, and make it fine underneath and drawing upwards:[INT](Note: I noticed that there are no line breaks in the original text. Here I will add them to make it easier to read.)
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Not too deeply, in order to hold it with the finger, and press gently
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the enema syringe
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	An enema is never made with a silver or copper syringe, or with melted tin or iron; and sometimes they are made with these instruments, large or small, depending on who they are prepared for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, those who are used in the care of children and infirm adults are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small and large enema syringe is broad at the top, where the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and there should be an opening where the belly is tied, as you see, and the intestines inside perforated; and it should have two openings on one side, and one on the other.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	And let the belly, where one puts medicine from an animal bladder or parchment, be pierced all around with small holes.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	And let there be a space the size of a finger between each hole, then insert into these holes a strong thread twisted in ten or twelve strands, and bind the belly like a corset.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then administer an enema; and this is the method of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the tip of the enema with oil or egg yolk, or a similar substance, then insert it gently.[Instructions for administering an enema in a medieval medical treatise. The text advises to prepare a belly "belly" or bladder containing medicine, which should be bound around the patient's waist with a corset-like binding. The medicine should not be too hot or too cold. The tip of the enema should be coated in oil or egg yolk before gently inserting it into the patient. The text also specifies that the holes in the belly/bladder should be small and spaced one finger-width apart, and that a strong twisted thread should be inserted into these holes to help hold the binding in place.]
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then the minister presses it with both hands until it is emptied, then removes the enema and lifts the patient's legs in the air.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to come out, let it do so as much as it can; and if he sleeps for a whole night, it will be a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give an enema to a patient with a disorder of the belly, and the medicine quickly comes out, re-administer it until it is clear that it has taken effect.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are in or around the anus, let the enema be as gentle as for a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the gentle enema, with the skin stretched tight:
des plaies	from wounds[STHAPPY]
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have previously said in the division the cure for wounds; now we will tell you the cures for hands and remedies, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are: striking with a stone, cutting with a sword or knife, or with a spear or stick, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	Or according to the parts of the body where the wounds are located, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members.[ST1]
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	And I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, for the reminder will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound occurs to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a blow of a stone or similar things, and the skin is still torn and the wound is large.
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and if you suspect a hot abscess: make it drain immediately from the same head (cephalic) itself if there is only a little blood coming out of the wound, and let the incision be on the opposite side of the injured part.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and avoid giving food and drink to the patient that is heavy and difficult to digest, such as wine and meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he refuses to let it drain, then lighten his food, and let him not drink wine or eat meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	And place on the wound, if a hot abscess should arise, cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in stiptic wine.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, place [the cautery] on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been moved by air or powder, which I will speak of a little later;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has been moved by pus, place some ointments on it until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a cut from a sword or similar, and the lips cannot come together with bandages, then bring them together with stitches, as I will say for wounds of the belly, through stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and hangs, and only holds on by a little, then cut it; then cure the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And command the patient to eat hearty foods, such as meat and roasted wheat, like fowl, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find a rotten spot on the skin that does not adhere to the bone, cut it out and throw it away, then proceed to cure it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, without a visible cut, and it cannot be stopped with medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if that does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if the wounds are small and simple, then the cure is easy: which is to apply this powder that coagulates once the arrow has moved it.[NOTE: I'm assuming "ars" is a typo and should be "aros" (arrows).]
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	The way to make the powder is: take one part of incense, two parts of dragon's blood, three parts of quicklime, and grind it into a fine powder.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and treat the wound, and bind it firmly, until it dries out and connects with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then bind it securely, and leave it unbound if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with lime alone, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but the physician has dried out the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the physician has dried out the wound, one should not put this powder on it at all.[INTRODUCING NEW TOPIC...]:
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some digestive ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it becomes loose;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal other injuries until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if a fracture of the bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with delicate forceps;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about skull fractures.
de la plaie dou col	about the wound in the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, except if the sinew or artery of the neck is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the sinew, there is no other means than to leave the wound alone and not apply any restricting substance, for this is harmful to the sinews and causes them to retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	And do not place anything cold on the wound, for the substance of sinews is cold and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	But let the medicine be warm, such as chalk washed in fresh water and mixed with rose oil, and also lettuce boiled in fresh water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	And other stones of this kind, as well as moist ointments.[ST1]
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, let it be sewn and bandaged, and leave it to heal until it is healed.[ST1]
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and swollen with pus, lance them or cut lower at a different spot;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if an artery is cut and bleeding comes out of it, tie it off, and if necessary, cauterize it.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	And if the spine of the throat or the windpipe is cut, and the passage remains intact through which food goes;
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	Then place the windpipe on a reed, but do not touch the throat and put it back in its natural shape.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then bandage it appropriately and leave it for some days, then cure it with decoctions until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has impressed on the bone, soothe it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are bone fragments, pull all of them out if you can, and those that you cannot, leave until the wound rots.[* a more modern translation would be "and if there are bone fragments, remove as many as you can, and those that you cannot, leave until the wound heals"*]
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and let the wound be opened and aligned properly.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle powder on it that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is also a fistula, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a strike from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, look to see if any foul wind comes out of the wound when the patient exhales; then you will know that the wound is deadly.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	And if it is not deep and the wound is completely fresh with blood, do not apply powder immediately or bind it up at first, so that the blood can flow freely.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and return (the blood) to the heart, hurry and care for the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but apply an attractive ointment, and bind it up two times a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	And if you don't have any ointment, put old cotton in the wound to soak up the moisture.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	And make the patient sleep on the wound for 3 days, or 4, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	so that there will not come any spasm, nor bad tremors of the heart, nor twitchings of the sinews;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	And when you see good signs, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure it with bandages and other treatments, until it is healed.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	And if it cannot heal and becomes operative, immediately realize that there is a fistula; then cure it as one should. (My translation)
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut and it is simple, whether it's on the belly or back, then heal the part in front of it;

ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because corruption is a form of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or due to the property in the region where digestion is slow, health is delayed, and it is naturally swollen;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or if there are veins or bones;
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, as well as their signs and cures, in the division (section).
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary for me to let you know the treatment of fistula, which is performed by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula can happen in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from the great veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or in the syphilitic sore, or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or in some of the ribs,[
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or in the spine of the back, or in any joints of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and some reach the root of the main member and to similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas of this kind are of difficult healing, and there is only labor and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	And if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have mentioned, and you are confident in the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	And if you see it (the fistula), then take a probe of steel or iron, and if the fistula is straight, seek (it) out.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	And if the fistula is twisted, then search for it with a slender probe of lead.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	For lead bends easily around the twisting (of the fistula).[INT](Note: I will provide the next sentence in another message because it exceeds the character limit)
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	And if the fistula has many holes and you cannot fully encircle it with probes,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	then irrigate it through one of the holes,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for moisture is quickly transferred from one hole to another, thus cleansing it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	Then try to extract blood to the best of your ability, so you can determine if there is bone or nerve involved, and if it runs deep,[ST1]
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	And carefully ask the patient about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and where they feel it;[ST1]
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from the joint, or nerve, or artery or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I have told you, then adjust it according to what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the abscess and corrupt flesh that are inside,
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then treat it until it has healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is deep and straight, then you must cauterize as deeply as possible.
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then insert dampened wicks in the wound, and push them up to the head of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine consumes the excess matter that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then apply heated plasters of clean flesh until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	And if it does not heal with this method, cauterize it as we have said.
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if the bone is corrupt due to the fistula, then amputate it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If vein or sinew does not trouble you or the principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	And if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, soak it until all the corruption is removed,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure it with healing things, until the flesh is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed and becomes bowed as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not yet reached the root (of the problem).
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if you uncover and search until you are at the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore it to its place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, it is good.[
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot reach it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	there is no other remedy but to let nature take its course;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	And if there is a small broken bone, and you can pull it out with tongs,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	then extract it with a suitable instrument for that purpose,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, pull them all out, do not leave even one.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	And if moisture (pus) is opposed to it, and there is no mistake or fear,[IST] si le fais bouillir en ewe cler;
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	Then cut out the pus and flesh, and free the bones (from them).
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place a corrupting agent on the wound.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it until the area around the bones becomes corrupt.
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And then the bones will more easily come out;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	And if it is one of the large bones, such as the thigh bone or leg bone,[INTERNET] {start article}
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	only allow the corruption to continue long enough for all the blackness to disappear,[INTERNET] {start article}
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if a large part of it is corrupt, and reaches down to the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	it must be covered and protected up to the corruption, and then cured until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you can take an example and help in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was a young man around thirty years old, who had pain in his leg due to something that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	until the matter reached the leg and he was swollen with a large abscess, and there was no apparent reason to open it;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the foolish surgeons operated on him so much that the abscess burst,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and a lot of matter was coming out, and it became a fistula, and many holes formed that all drained corrupt and moist matter from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	"And many experts spent two years trying to heal it, and there was no wise person in the healing art."
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	"as long as I was called there and saw his leg and the medications used to heal it,"
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	"and what ran through the openings of a large body;"
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	"and the young man's flesh became red and had a citron-colored hue."
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	"I set up a tent in one of these openings, and then searched all the openings,"[irst](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/premier) line of text:
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	And I found that one came against the other from all the parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	So I hurried and cut into one of the holes until I exposed a part of the bone.
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	And I found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption went all the way to the inside bone;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I thought that what appeared to me of the rotten bone was all the corruption, except for what I removed;[5](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/cuidai#fr)
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	And I began to heal the wound with soaking medicines for a long time, and it could not heal.[6](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/soud#fr)
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then begin again, and uncover the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and scraped it off, and then removed it, and took care to heal the wound.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not manage to remove more than a palm's width of the bone, and extracted it all the way down to the marrow.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored it with medicine, and it was quickly healed and fused.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and there was no need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it. The first sentence translates to "and then begin again, and uncover the bone as before," indicating that the author is performing a medical procedure that involves uncovering a bone.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and due to the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For through the evacuation (of blood) he often groaned, but he was completely healed.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and in place of the bone, there grew a hard flesh, and he was of good disposition and had no trouble or contrary symptoms at all, either when walking or standing still.[In this context, "evacuation" refers to the removal or drainage of blood from a wound or abscess. The patient had been experiencing pain due to this evacuation, but was later healed completely.]
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if a bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this way:[This sentence indicates that the text will now discuss the treatment of broken bones. The word "soier" means "to heal" or "to treat."]
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take a ligament and bind it to the end of the bone that is visible,[This sentence describes the first step in treating a broken bone: binding a ligament to the visible end of the fractured bone. A ligament is a band of tough, elastic connective tissue that surrounds joints and supports or binds together other structures.]
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and instruct someone to stretch it out high;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and place another larger linen ligament, and tie it over the flesh that is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the head so that you pull out the rotten flesh beneath,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh above the wound where you see swelling, so that the swelling does not pierce the flesh;[INTUIT: "soie" here refers to a visible swelling or bump on the skin.]
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a splint or board under the bone, in order to cover the rotten flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and one must be cautious as long as one can see and feel the corruption, and be cautious again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupt and not visible, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	remove all the flesh; then place a splint underneath,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then sew through the length of the corruption, leaving a long thread on either side, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the corrupt joint and sew the bone that it surrounds on the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other solution but to cut (amputate).
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	And if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or the ankle of the foot, this is a very serious matter,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nonetheless, you must examine the corruption and see how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in every way that you can, except where the vein or nerve makes it difficult for you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	And know that there are many types of scalpels and needles for covering these bones, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of openings.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and fineness, their size and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And for this reason, you must prepare the appropriate tool for each type of work.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	And know that the work will show you the tool you will need, according to the knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and bear witness to the signs of the illnesses.[INST) The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you plan the instrument which you need according to what is required.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The heads (of abscesses) rot either from within or from without;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have treated this corruption with the help of medicines, but they do not help at all,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then you should cover that limb until the place where the corruption comes from.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient escapes from death by this, or from the greater evil, which is the defect of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and one of the signs is that the limb becomes black, as if it has been burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and follows the blackness, then this corruption spreads from member to member.

et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is due to the bite of some poisonous animals, such as a sea scorpion, a viper, and similar creatures,[INTERNAL\_ERROR]
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If the corruption is on the head of the arm, cut it out and do not allow it to reach as far as the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes as far as the hand, cut it at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	And if it comes to the arm, cut with a knife, and if it passes the knife, it is deadly.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	And no appeasement will be of any use unless it matches the amount of its strength.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	And do similarly when the corruption comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, cut after the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	And if it [the dislocation] comes to the foot, cut off the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	And if it [the dislocation] rises to the leg, cut at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it [the dislocation] comes above the knee, there is no other means but to let the patient die;[intval ignored, line skipped:  ]et s'elle vient desus le genoil, si n'i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	And the way to cut off a member, whether with a knife or scissors, is to bind it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	And have one minister stretch one of the lower bandages tight, and another minister stretch the other bandage above,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you cut through the flesh that is between the two ligaments with a spatula wide, so that the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then the piece of flesh or suture, and place a linen cloth on each side, so that the suture does not touch the healthy area,
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and the patient comes to harm with another injury and abscess caused by this.[Source](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lanfranc_de_Milan#cite_ref-2)
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding occurs while you are working, then quickly cauterize the area.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or apply some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is completed.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and cure it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you that it happened to one man in a deep sleep:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he experienced a nightmare that resembled a burn from fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and this corruption first appeared on his big toe of the foot, spreading to the entire foot;[ISTM] et puis s’en ala a ses autres piez et a ses mains, et fu si grant k’ele li fist morir.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the man saw the corruption, he immediately put a covering on his foot, and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	And for a long time after, the ulcer or finger of the hand returned, and it came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I applied soothing things to it after cleaning the wound, but the ulcer could not heal;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted me to amputate his hand, but I did not want to, as I had hope of healing the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he might die;
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for his vitality was weak; and he despaired completely, and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	And if he covers his hand with a glove, and is healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I do not mention this except that one does it in order to use it when necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes in a fleshy place and remains so long that it forms a large collection of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	And then it bursts and breaks open, and the pus comes out, leaving the place empty like a vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	And the skin on top is as thin as a delicate piece of cloth,[STHAPUS]{provided\_context}|
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and they do not run up to the bone, nor up to the nerve, and such a disease is called "sana" (modern French: saine), presumably a variant of the Old French word "san" meaning healthy or sound. However, it seems there is a mistake in the text as "sain" or "san" does not mean "dislocation" in Old French. The rest of the sentence and context do not provide enough information to correct this potential error. Here's the corrected translation:
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called a "fistula" either.
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	But if it becomes so elongated that it reaches the bone deeply, it is then called a "fistula".[Text written in Old French around the 12th-13th centuries discussing the treatment of dislocations.](https://i.imgur.com/gallery/PQB85aZ)
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is such that you cut all around it, and similarly when it is thin, like a piece of cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and not be afraid of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you suspect that the skin has hardened, but corruption is not yet present,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and if the skin is thick with flesh, then cure it with an enema as follows:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look to see if the breasts are swollen, and if the belly that contains it has a foul smell,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then enema with an Egyptian medicine which is made as follows:[not sure about the "e" in front of egyptian. I assume it's a typo and remove it]
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take easel, and oil, and litharge equally, and put to cook in one vessel over fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine becomes red and thickens as much as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take some of this as needed, and mix it with water and honey.
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and use it as an enema for the lung, while constricting the anus.
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then extract it by straining.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Perform this many times, until the breast is emptied and the pus is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and at times, perform a cleansing enema with water and ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you should take ashes from a grapevine log, and pour water over it,

This is a description of varicose veins, which were not well understood in medieval medicine but were recognized as a condition characterized by swelling and bulging veins. The "superfluitez melancoliouses" likely refers to an excess of black bile or melancholy humor, which was thought to accumulate in the body and cause various health problems.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And this occurs more frequently in the legs of those who walk or work and carry heavy loads than in others. This is an accurate observation as varicose veins tend to be more common in people who are on their feet for long periods of time, such as laborers and farmers. The increased pressure on the leg veins from standing and working can cause them to become swollen and enlarged over time, leading to the development of varicose veins.
